titles)</small></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.sixnationsrugby.com">www<wbr />.sixnationsrugby<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Six Nations Championship</b> (recently known as the <b>NatWest 6 Nations</b> for sponsorship reasons) is an annual international <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> competition between the teams of <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_rugby_union_team" title="Italy national rugby union team">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Scotland national rugby union team">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_union_team" title="Wales national rugby union team">Wales</a>. The current champions are Ireland, having won the <a href="/wiki/2018_Six_Nations_Championship" title="2018 Six Nations Championship">2018 tournament</a>.\n</p><p>The Six Nations is the successor to the Home Nations Championship (1883\xe2\x80\x931909 and 1932\xe2\x80\x9339), played between teams from England, Ireland, Scotland and Wales, which was the first international rugby union tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-Godwin1_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Godwin1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> With the addition of France, this became the Five Nations Championship (1910\xe2\x80\x9331 and 1947\xe2\x80\x9399), which in turn became the Six Nations Championship with the addition of Italy. \n</p><p>England hold the record for outright wins of the Home Nations, Five Nations and Six Nations tournaments, with 28 titles, although Wales follow closely with 26 outright wins with the addition of 12 shared victories to England\'s 10. Since the Six Nations era started in 2000, only Italy and Scotland have failed to win the Six Nations title, although Scotland were the last winners of the Five Nations.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" <span class="toctext">Sponsorship</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_expansion">History and expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History and expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The tournament was first played in 1883 as the Home Nations Championship among the four Home Nations \xe2\x80\x94 England, Ireland, Scotland, and Wales. The tournament then became the Five Nations Championship in 1910 with the addition of France. The tournament was expanded in 2000 to become the Six Nations Championship with the addition of Italy.\n</p><p>Following the relative success of the Tier 2 nations in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015 Rugby World Cup</a>, there were calls by <a href="/wiki/Octavian_Morariu" title="Octavian Morariu">Octavian Morariu</a>, the president of Rugby Union\'s governing body for promotion and development, to let <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Georgia national rugby union team">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_rugby_union_team" title="Romania national rugby union team">Romania</a> join the Six Nations due to their consistent success in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Europe_International_Championships" title="Rugby Europe International Championships">European Nations Cup</a> and ability to compete in the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Format">Format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tournoi2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tournoi2.svg/220px-Tournoi2.svg.png" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tournoi2.svg/330px-Tournoi2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Tournoi2.svg/440px-Tournoi2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="578" data-file-height="641" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tournoi2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The locations of the Six Nations participants</div></div></div>\n<p>Played annually, the format of the Championship is simple: each team plays every other team once (making a total of 15 matches), with home ground advantage alternating from one year to the next. Prior to the 2017 tournament, two points were awarded for a win, one for a draw and none for a loss. Unlike many other rugby union competitions the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_bonus_points_system" title="Rugby union bonus points system">bonus point system</a> has not previously been used.\n</p><p>On 30 November 2016, the 6 Nations Committee announced that the bonus point system will be trialled for the 2017 Championship. The system is similar to the one used in most rugby championships (0 points for a loss, 2 for a draw, 4 for a win, 1 for scoring four or more tries in match, and 1 for losing by 7 points or fewer), with the only difference being that a Grand Slam winner will be given 3 extra points to ensure they finish top of the table. \n</p><p>Prior to 1994, teams equal on match points shared the championship. Since then, ties have been broken by considering the points difference of the teams. The rules of the championship further provide that if teams tie on both match points and points difference, the team that scored the most tries wins the championship. Were this decider to be a tie, the tying teams would share the championship.<sup id="cite_ref-rules_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> To date, however, match points and points difference have been sufficient to decide the championship.\n</p><p>Also, the team that finishes at the bottom of the league table is said to have "won" the <a href="/wiki/Wooden_Spoon_(rugby_union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wooden Spoon (rugby union)">Wooden Spoon</a>, although no actual trophy is given to the team. A team that has lost all five matches is said to have been <a href="/wiki/Whitewash_(sport)" title="Whitewash (sport)">whitewashed</a>. Since the inaugural Six Nations tournament in 2000, only England and Ireland have avoided the Wooden Spoon award. Italy are the holders of the most Wooden Spoon awards in the Six Nations era with eleven, and have been whitewashed six times. However, each of the other five nations has accumulated more than that through competing in previous eras.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophies">Trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Championship_Trophy">Championship Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Championship Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg/220px-Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg/330px-Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg/440px-Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ireland_2009_6_nations_triple_crown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Original Six Nations Championship Trophy (1993\xe2\x80\x932014) and The Triple Crown Trophy</div></div></div>\n<p>The winners of the Six Nations are presented with the Championship Trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-trophy_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trophy-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> This was originally conceived by the <a href="/wiki/David_Anthony_Thomas_Fane,_15th_Earl_of_Westmorland" class="mw-redirect" title="David Anthony Thomas Fane, 15th Earl of Westmorland">Earl of Westmorland</a>, and was first presented to the winners of the 1993 championship, France. It is a <a href="/wiki/Sterling_silver" title="Sterling silver">sterling silver</a> trophy, designed by James Brent-Ward and made by a team of eight silversmiths from the London firm William Comyns.\n</p><p>It has 15 side panels representing the 15 members of the team and with three handles to represent the three officials (referee and two touch judges). The cup has a capacity of 3.75 litres \xe2\x80\x93 sufficient for five bottles of champagne. Within the mahogany base is a concealed drawer which contains six alternate <a href="/wiki/Finial" title="Finial">finials</a>, each a silver replica of one of the team emblems, which can be screwed on the detachable lid.\n</p><p>A new trophy was introduced for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Six_Nations_Championship" title="2015 Six Nations Championship">2015 Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\t\nThe new trophy was designed and crafted by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lyte" title="Thomas Lyte">Thomas Lyte</a> silversmiths and replaces the 1993 edition, which is being retired as it represented the nations that took part in the Five Nations Championship. Ireland were the last team to win the old trophy, and coincidentally, the first team to win the new one.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Slam_and_Triple_Crown">Grand Slam and Triple Crown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Grand Slam and Triple Crown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A team that wins all its games wins the \'<a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(rugby_union)" title="Grand Slam (rugby union)">Grand Slam</a>\'. \n</p><p>Victory by any Home Nation over the other three <a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">Home Nations</a> is a \'<a href="/wiki/Triple_Crown_(rugby_union)" title="Triple Crown (rugby union)">Triple Crown</a>\'. Although this achievement has long been a feature of the tournament, it was not until 2006 that a physical Triple Crown trophy was awarded.\n</p><p>The Triple Crown may only be won by England, Ireland, Scotland or Wales, when one nation wins all three of their matches against the others, during the Six Nations Championship. The Triple Crown honour has long been a feature of the tournament, dating back to the original Home Nations Championship, but the physical Triple Crown Trophy has been awarded only since 2006. The current holder of the Triple Crown is Ireland, who defeated England, Scotland, and Wales in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Six_Nations_Championship" title="2016 Six Nations Championship">2018 championship</a>. For the 2006 Six Nations, the Royal Bank of Scotland (the primary sponsor of the competition) commissioned Hamilton &amp; Inches to design and create a dedicated Triple Crown Trophy. It has since been won three times by Ireland and twice by England and Wales.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_trophies">Rivalry trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rivalry trophies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several individual competitions take place under the umbrella of the tournament. The oldest such regular competition is for the <a href="/wiki/Calcutta_Cup" title="Calcutta Cup">Calcutta Cup</a>, contested annually between England and Scotland since 1879. It is named the Calcutta Cup as it is made from melted-down Indian Rupees donated by the Calcutta Club. Since 1988, the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Trophy" title="Millennium Trophy">Millennium Trophy</a> has been awarded to the winner of the game between England and Ireland, and since 1989 the <a href="/wiki/Centenary_Quaich" title="Centenary Quaich">Centenary Quaich</a> has been awarded to the winner of the game between Ireland and Scotland. Since 2007, France and Italy have contested the <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi_Trophy" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi Trophy">Giuseppe Garibaldi Trophy</a>; it was created for the 200th anniversary of the birth of <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, the Italian hero who helped unify Italy and volunteered in the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Vosges" title="Army of the Vosges">French Republican Army</a> against Prussia.\n</p><p>The following trophies are contested within the main competition, mostly as long-standing fixtures between pairs of teams:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Calcutta_Cup" title="Calcutta Cup">Calcutta Cup</a> \xe2\x80\x93 contested annually between England and Scotland since 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-CalcuttaCup_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CalcuttaCup-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Millennium_Trophy" title="Millennium Trophy">Millennium Trophy</a> \xe2\x80\x93 contested annually between England and Ireland since 1988, presented to celebrate Dublin\'s millennium in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-RFUAboutUs_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFUAboutUs-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Centenary_Quaich" title="Centenary Quaich">Centenary Quaich</a> \xe2\x80\x93 contested annually between Ireland and Scotland since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-NeverIresQuaich_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NeverIresQuaich-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QuaichAnnual_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuaichAnnual-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-quaich_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quaich-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi_Trophy" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi Trophy">Giuseppe Garibaldi Trophy</a> \xe2\x80\x93 contested annually between France and Italy since 2007, in memory of <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>, leader in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">unification of Italy</a> and volunteer in the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Vosges" title="Army of the Vosges">French Republican Army</a> against <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.</li></ul>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Auld_Alliance_Trophy" title="Auld Alliance Trophy">Auld Alliance Trophy</a> \xe2\x80\x93 contested annually between France and Scotland since 2018, in memory of the war dead from the rugby communities of Scotland and France.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg/200px-Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg/300px-Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg/400px-Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="469" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aviva_Stadium_from_North_Stand.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Stadium" title="Aviva Stadium">Aviva Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As of the 2019 competition, Six Nations matches are held in the following stadia:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Team\n</th>\n<th>Stadium\n</th>\n<th>Capacity\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_union_team" title="England national rugby union team">England</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center">82,000\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">France</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Stade_de_France" title="Stade de France">Stade de France</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center">81,338\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_union_team" title="Wales national rugby union team">Wales</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Principality_Stadium" national rugby union team">Italy</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico" title="Stadio Olimpico">Stadio Olimpico</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center">72,698\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Scotland national rugby union team">Scotland</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Murrayfield_Stadium" title="Murrayfield Stadium">Murrayfield Stadium</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center">67,144\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Ireland</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Aviva_Stadium" title="Aviva Stadium">Aviva Stadium</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:center">51,700\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The opening of the Aviva Stadium in May 2010 ended the arrangement with the <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> (GAA) that allowed the all-Ireland governing body for rugby union, the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Irish Rugby Football Union">Irish Rugby Football Union</a>, to use the GAA\'s flagship stadium, <a href="/wiki/Croke_Park" title="Croke Park">Croke Park</a>, for its international matches. This arrangement was made necessary by the 2007 closure and subsequent demolition of Ireland\'s traditional home at <a href="/wiki/Lansdowne_Road" title="Lansdowne Road">Lansdowne Road</a>; the Aviva was built on the former Lansdowne Road site. During the construction of the Aviva, Croke Park was the largest of the Six Nations grounds, with a capacity of 82,300.\n</p><p>In 2012 Italy moved their home games from the Stadio Flaminio, which only held 32,000, to the Stadio Olimpico, also in Rome, with a capacity of 72,000. \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Rugby_Federation" title="French Rugby Federation">French Rugby Federation</a> (FFR) had planned to build a new stadium of its own, seating 82,000 in the southern suburbs of Paris,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> because of frustrations with their tenancy of the Stade de France.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_FFR_stadium_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_FFR_stadium-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However the project was cancelled in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Results">Results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Results">edit</a><span data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Stockdale" title="Jacob Stockdale">Jacob Stockdale</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Six_Nations_Championship_records" title="List of Six Nations Championship records">List of Six Nations Championship records</a></div>\n<p>England\'s <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Wilkinson" title="Jonny Wilkinson">Jonny Wilkinson</a> currently holds the records for individual points in one match (35 points against Italy in 2001) and one season with 89 (scored in 2001). <a href="/wiki/Ronan_O%27Gara" title="Ronan O&#39;Gara">Ronan O\'Gara</a> of Ireland holds the career scoring record with 557 points to Wilkinson\'s 546, having surpassed Wilkinson in Round 3 of the 2011 championship.\n</p><p>The record for tries in a match is held by Scotsman <a href="/wiki/George_Campbell_Lindsay" title="George Campbell Lindsay">George Lindsay</a> who scored five tries against Wales in 1887.<sup id="cite_ref-SNrecords_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNrecords-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> England\'s <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Lowe" title="Cyril Lowe">Cyril Lowe</a> and Scotland\'s <a href="/wiki/Ian_Smith_(Scottish_rugby_player_born_1903)" title="Ian Smith (Scottish rugby player born 1903)">Ian Smith</a> jointly hold the record for tries in one season with 8 (Lowe in 1914, Smith in 1925). Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/Brian_O%27Driscoll" title="Brian O&#39;Driscoll">Brian O\'Driscoll</a> has the Championship record for tries with 26.\n</p><p>The record for appearances is held by O\'Gara, with 63 Six Nations appearances from the start of the Six Nations era in 2000 to his retirement in 2013. He surpassed countryman <a href="/wiki/Mike_Gibson_(rugby_player)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mike Gibson (rugby player)">Mike Gibson</a> in the first round of the 2012 tournament against Wales. Gibson played in 56 Five Nations matches (Italy had not become part of the Championship yet) between 1964 and 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-SNrecords_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNrecords-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most points scored by a team in one match was 80 points, scored by England against Italy in 2001. England also scored the most ever points in a season in 2001 with 229, and most tries in a season with 29.<sup id="cite_ref-SNrecords_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNrecords-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Wales hold the record for fewest tries conceded during a season in the Six Nations era, conceding only 2 in 5 games in 2008, but the 1977 Grand Slam-winning France team did not concede a try in their four matches. Wales hold the record for the longest time without conceding a try, at 358 minutes in the 2013 tournament.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_television_contracts">Administration and television contracts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administration and television contracts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Championship is run from headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> by Six Nations Rugby Ltd,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> which also takes responsibility for the <a href="/wiki/British_and_Irish_Lions" title="British and Irish Lions">British and Irish Lions</a> tours. The CEO of the Championship is John Feehan, a former Leinster player. \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> has long covered the tournament, broadcasting all matches apart from England home matches between 1997 and 2002, which were shown live by Sky Sports with highlights on the BBC.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Between 2003 and 2015, the BBC covered every match live on BBC Sport either on BBC One or BBC Two with highlights also on the BBC Sport website and either on the BBC Red Button or late at night on BBC Two. In 2011, it was announced that the BBC\'s coverage of the tournament on TV, radio and online would be extended to 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> However, on 9 July 2015, in reaction to <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">satellite</a> <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">pay-TV</a> bids from <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> for coverage from 2017, BBC agreed to lose exclusive rights to the tournament two years early. But from 2016, BBC and <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> would jointly broadcast the tournament in the UK, with BBC showing all France, Scotland and Wales home matches live, and ITV showing all England, Ireland and Italy home matches live.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> This means that the Six Nations will remain on free-to-air television in the UK until 2021.\n</p><p>In Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann" title="Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann">RT\xc3\x89</a> have broadcast the championship since RT\xc3\x89\'s inception and continued to do so until 2017, while <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a> televised highlights. However in late 2015 it was announced that free to air rival TV3 would take over the rights for every game from the Six Nations on Irish Television from 2018\xe2\x80\x932021, so that after the 2017 championship RT\xc3\x89 lost the rights.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/France_T%C3%A9l%C3%A9visions" title="France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9visions">France T\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa9visions</a> covered the competition in France; this lasted until 2017.\n</p><p>In Italy, from 2014 to 2017 <a href="/wiki/DMAX_(Italy)" title="DMAX (Italy)">DMAX</a> of <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery Communications">Discovery Communications</a> broadcast all matches, and will do so until 2021.\n</p><p>In the United States, <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a> broadcasts matches in English and <a href="/wiki/TV5_Monde" class="mw-redirect" title="TV5 Monde">TV5 Monde</a> airs matches in French.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a> also broadcasts matches featuring the Welsh team shown by the BBC in <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Until 1998, the Championship had no <a href="/wiki/Title_sponsor" class="mw-redirect" title="Title sponsor">title sponsor</a>. Sponsorship rights were sold to <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Bank" title="Lloyds Bank">Lloyds TSB</a> for the 1999 tournament and the competition was titled the <b>Lloyds TSB 5 Nations</b> and <b>Lloyds TSB 6 Nations</b> until 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland_Group" title="Royal Bank of Scotland Group">Royal Bank of Scotland Group</a> took over sponsorship from 2004 until 2017, with the competition being branded the <b>RBS 6 Nations</b>. A new title sponsor was sought for the 2018 tournament and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> However, after struggling to find a new sponsor, organisers agreed a one-year extension with the Royal Bank of Scotland Group at a reduced rate. As the RBS initials brand was being phased out, the tournament was named after their banking arm <a href="/wiki/NatWest" title="NatWest">NatWest</a>, becoming the <b>Natwest 6 Nations</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Six_Nations_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span
